 <p>\n       <b>\n        Cape Verde\n       </b>\n       (\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">\n         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">\n          /\n          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">\n           <span title="/\xcb\x8c/: secondary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x8c\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'k\' in \'kind\'">\n            k\n           </span>\n           <span title="/e\xc9\xaa/: \'a\' in \'face\'">\n            e\xc9\xaa\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'p\' in \'pie\'">\n            p\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">\n           <span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x88\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'v\' in \'vie\'">\n            v\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x9c\xcb\x90r/: \'ur\' in \'fur\'">\n            \xc9\x9c\xcb\x90r\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'d\' in \'dye\'">\n            d\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          /\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       ) or\n       <b>\n        Cabo Verde\n       </b>\n       (\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">\n         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">\n          /\n          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">\n           <span title="/\xcb\x8c/: secondary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x8c\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'k\' in \'kind\'">\n            k\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x91\xcb\x90/: \'a\' in \'father\'">\n            \xc9\x91\xcb\x90\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'b\' in \'buy\'">\n            b\n           </span>\n           <span title="/o\xca\x8a/: \'o\' in \'code\'">\n            o\xca\x8a\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">\n           <span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x88\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'v\' in \'vie\'">\n            v\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x9c\xcb\x90r/: \'ur\' in \'fur\'">\n            \xc9\x9c\xcb\x90r\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'d\' in \'dye\'">\n            d\n           </span>\n           <span title="/e\xc9\xaa/: \'a\' in \'face\'">\n            e\xc9\xaa\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          /\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       ,\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">\n         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">\n          /\n          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">\n           <span title="/\xcb\x8c/: secondary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x8c\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'k\' in \'kind\'">\n            k\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc3\xa6/: \'a\' in \'bad\'">\n            \xc3\xa6\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'b\' in \'buy\'">\n            b\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          -/\n         </a>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       ) (\n       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">\n        Portuguese\n       </a>\n       :\n       <span lang="pt">\n        <i>\n         Cabo Verde\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       ,\n       <small>\n        pronounced\n       </small>\n       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">\n        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Portuguese" title="Help:IPA/Portuguese">\n         [\xcb\x88ka\xce\xb2u \xcb\x88ve\xc9\xbe\xc3\xb0\xc9\xa8]\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       ), officially the\n       <b>\n        Republic of Cabo Verde\n       </b>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NameNatGeo_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NameNatGeo-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       is an\n       <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">\n        island country\n       </a>\n       spanning an\n       <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">\n        archipelago\n       </a>\n       of 10\n       <a href="/wiki/High_island" title="High island">\n        volcanic islands\n       </a>\n       in the central\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">\n        Atlantic Ocean\n       </a>\n       . Located 570 kilometres (350\xc2\xa0mi) west of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Verde_Peninsula" title="Cape Verde Peninsula">\n        Cape Verde Peninsula\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">\n        West Africa\n       </a>\n       , the islands cover a combined area of slightly over 4,000 square kilometres (1,500\xc2\xa0sq\xc2\xa0mi).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Cape Verde archipelago was uninhabited until the 15th century, when\n       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">\n        Portuguese\n       </a>\n       explorers discovered and\n       <a href="/wiki/Colony" title="Colony">\n        colonized\n       </a>\n       the islands, establishing the first European settlement in the tropics. Ideally located for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">\n        Atlantic slave trade\n       </a>\n       , the islands grew prosperous throughout the 16th and 17th centuries, attracting merchants,\n       <a href="/wiki/Privateer" title="Privateer">\n        privateers\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Piracy" title="Piracy">\n        pirates\n       </a>\n       . The end of slavery in the 19th century led to economic decline and emigration. Cape Verde gradually recovered as an important commercial center and stopover for shipping routes. Incorporated as an overseas department of Portugal in 1951, the islands continued to agitate for independence, which was peacefully achieved in 1975.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Since the early 1990s, Cape Verde has been a stable\n       <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">\n        representative democracy\n       </a>\n       , and remains one of the most developed and democratic countries in Africa. Lacking natural resources, its developing economy is mostly service-oriented, with a growing focus on tourism and foreign investment. Its population of around 512,000 is mostly of mixed European, North African/Berber, Moorish, and sub-Saharan African heritage, and predominantly Roman Catholic, reflecting the legacy of Portuguese rule. A\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verdean_diaspora" title="Cape Verdean diaspora">\n        sizeable diaspora community\n       </a>\n       exists across the world, slightly outnumbering inhabitants on the islands.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Historically, the name "Cape Verde" has been used in English for the archipelago and, since independence in 1975, for the country. In 2013, the Cape Verdean government determined that the Portuguese designation\n       <i>\n        Cabo Verde\n       </i>\n       would henceforth be used for official purposes, such as at the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">\n        United Nations\n       </a>\n       , even in English contexts. Cape Verde is a member of the\n       <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">\n        African Union\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc"     </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25">\n           <a href="#Science_and_technology">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.8\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Science and technology\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26">\n           <a href="#Crime">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.9\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Crime\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27">\n         <a href="#Culture">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Culture\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28">\n           <a href="#Media">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Media\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29">\n           <a href="#Music">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Music\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30">\n           <a href="#Dance">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Dance\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31">\n           <a href="#Literature">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Literature\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32">\n           <a href="#Cinema">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.5\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Cinema\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33">\n           <a href="#Cuisine">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.6\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Cuisine\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34">\n           <a href="#Sports">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             7.7\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Sports\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35">\n         <a href="#Transport">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Transport\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36">\n           <a href="#Ports">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             8.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Ports\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-37">\n           <a href="#Airports">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             8.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Airports\n            </span>\n           </a>\n           <ul>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-38">\n             <a href="#International_airports">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               8.2.1\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               International airports\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           9\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-40">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           10\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-41">\n         <a href="#Bibliography">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           11\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Bibliography\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-42">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           12\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">\n        Etymology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The name of the country stems from the nearby\n       <a href="/wiki/Cap-Vert" title="Cap-Vert">\n        Cap-Vert\n       </a>\n       , on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">\n        Senegalese\n       </a>\n       coast.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 1444 Portuguese explorers had named that landmark as\n       <i>\n        Cabo Verde,\n       </i>\n       a few years before they discovered the islands (\n       <i>\n        Verde\n       </i>\n       is\n       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">\n        Portuguese\n       </a>\n       for "green").\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 24 October 2013, the country\'s delegation announced at the United Nations that the official name should no longer be translated into other languages. Instead of "Cape Verde", the designation "Republic of Cabo Verde" is to be used.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NameNatGeo_9-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NameNatGeo-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Cape_Verde" title="History of Cape Verde">\n        History of Cape Verde\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Insulae_Capitis_viridis-1598.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1438" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Insulae_Capitis_viridis-1598.jpg/250px-Insulae_Capitis_viridis-1598.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Insulae_Capitis_viridis-1598.jpg/375px-Insulae_Capitis_viridis-1598.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Insulae_Capitis_viridis-1598.jpg/500px-Insulae_Capitis_viridis-1598.jpg 2x" width="250"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Insulae_Capitis_viridis-1598.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          Insulae Capitis Viridis\n         </i>\n         (1598), showing Cape Verde\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Before the arrival of Europeans, the Cape Verde Islands were uninhabited.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The islands of the Cape Verde archipelago were discovered by\n       <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">\n        Genoese\n       </a>\n       and Portuguese\n       <a href="/wiki/Navigator" title="Navigator">\n        navigators\n       </a>\n       around 1456. According to Portuguese official records,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the first discoveries were made by\n       <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">\n        Genoa\n       </a>\n       -born\n       <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_de_Noli" title="Ant\xc3\xb3nio de Noli">\n        Ant\xc3\xb3nio de Noli\n       </a>\n       , who was afterwards appointed governor of Cape Verde by Portuguese\n       <a href="/wiki/Afonso_V_of_Portugal" title="Afonso V of Portugal">\n        King Afonso V\n       </a>\n       . Other navigators mentioned as contributing to discoveries in the Cape Verde archipelago are\n       <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Gomes" title="Diogo Gomes">\n        Diogo Gomes\n       </a>\n       (who was with Ant\xc3\xb3nio de Noli and claimed to have been the first to land on and name Santiago island),\n       <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Dias" title="Diogo Dias">\n        Diogo Dias\n       </a>\n       , Diogo Afonso and the Italian (Venice-born)\n       <a href="/wiki/Alvise_Cadamosto" title="Alvise Cadamosto">\n        Alvise Cadamosto\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1462, Portuguese settlers arrived at\n       <a href="/wiki/Santiago,_Cape_Verde" title="Santiago, Cape Verde">\n        Santiago\n       </a>\n       and founded a settlement they called Ribeira Grande (now called\n       <a href="/wiki/Cidade_Velha" title="Cidade Velha">\n        Cidade Velha\n       </a>\n       , to avoid being confused with the town of\n       <a href="/wiki/Ribeira_Grande,_Cape_Verde" title="Ribeira Grande, Cape Verde">\n        Ribeira Grande\n       </a>\n       on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Santo_Ant%C3%A3o,_Cape_Verde" title="Santo Ant\xc3\xa3o, Cape Verde">\n        Santo Ant\xc3\xa3o\n       </a>\n       island). Ribeira Grande was the first permanent European settlement in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Tropics" title="Tropics">\n        tropics\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn_14-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bn-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mindelo-MontCara2000.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1378" data-file-width="3112" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Mindelo-MontCara2000.jpg/250px-Mindelo-MontCara2000.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Mindelo-MontCara2000.jpg/375px-Mindelo-MontCara2000.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Mindelo-MontCara2000.jpg/500px-Mindelo-MontCara2000.jpg 2x" width="250"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mindelo-MontCara2000.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A view of\n         <a href="/wiki/Monte_Cara" title="Monte Cara">\n          Monte Cara\n         </a>\n         from\n         <a href="/wiki/Mindelo" title="Mindelo">\n          Mindelo\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In the 16th century, the archipelago prospered from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">\n        Atlantic slave trade\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn_14-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bn-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Pirates occasionally attacked the Portuguese settlements. Sir\n       <a href="/wiki/Francis_Drake" title="Francis Drake">\n        Francis Drake\n       </a>\n       , an English corsair\n       <a href="/wiki/Privateer" title="Privateer">\n        privateering\n       </a>\n       under a\n       <a href="/wiki/Letter_of_marque" title="Letter of marque">\n        letter of marque\n       </a>\n       granted by the English crown, twice sacked the (then) capital\n       <a href="/wiki/Cidade_Velha" title="Cidade Velha">\n        Ribeira Grande\n       </a>\n       in 1585 when it was a part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">\n        Iberian Union\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn_14-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bn-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       After a French attack in 1712, the town declined in importance relative to nearby\n       <a href="/wiki/Praia" title="Praia">\n        Praia\n       </a>\n       , which became the capital in 1770.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn_14-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bn-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Decline in the slave trade in the 19th century resulted in an economic crisis. Cape Verde\'s early prosperity slowly vanished. However, the islands\' position astride mid-Atlantic shipping lanes made Cape Verde an ideal location for re-supplying ships. Because of its excellent harbour, the city of\n       <a href="/wiki/Mindelo" title="Mindelo">\n        Mindelo\n       </a>\n       , located on the island of\n       <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Vicente,_Cape_Verde" title="S\xc3\xa3o Vicente, Cape Verde">\n        S\xc3\xa3o Vicente\n       </a>\n       , became an important commercial centre during the 19th century.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn_14-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bn-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Diplomat\n       <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Roberts_(diplomat)" title="Edmund Roberts (diplomat)">\n        Edmund Roberts\n       </a>\n       visited Cape Verde in 1832.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roberts_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Roberts-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Garthpool_SLV_AllanGreen.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="553" data-file-width="990" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Garthpool_SLV_AllanGreen.jpg/250px-Garthpool_SLV_AllanGreen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Garthpool_SLV_AllanGreen.jpg/375px-Garthpool_SLV_AllanGreen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Garthpool_SLV_AllanGreen.jpg/500px-Garthpool_SLV_AllanGreen.jpg 2x" width="250"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Garthpool_SLV_AllanGreen.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Grain Ship "Garthpool", wrecked at Boavista, Cape Verde, in 1928\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       With few natural resources and inadequate sustainable investment from the Portuguese, the citizens grew increasingly discontented with the colonial masters, who nevertheless refused to provide the local authorities with more autonomy. In 1951, Portugal changed Cape Verde\'s status from a colony to an overseas province in an attempt to blunt growing\n       <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">\n        nationalism\n       </a>\n       . In 1956,\n       <a href="/wiki/Am%C3%ADlcar_Cabral" title="Am\xc3\xadlcar Cabral">\n        Am\xc3\xadlcar Cabral\n       </a>\n       and a group of fellow Cape Verdeans and Guineans organised (in\n       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Guinea" title="Portuguese Guinea">\n        Portuguese Guinea\n       </a>\n       ) the clandestine\n       <a href="/wiki/African_Party_for_the_Independence_of_Guinea_and_Cape_Verde" title="African Party for the Independence of Guinea and Cape Verde">\n        African Party for the Independence of Guinea and Cape Verde\n       </a>\n       (PAIGC).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn_14-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bn-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       It demanded improvement in economic, social and political conditions in Cape Verde and Portuguese Guinea and formed the basis of the two nations\' independence movement. Moving its headquarters to\n       <a href="/wiki/Conakry" title="Conakry">\n        Conakry\n       </a>\n       , Guinea in 1960, the PAIGC began an armed rebellion against Portugal in 1961. Acts of sabotage eventually grew into a\n       <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau_War_of_Independence" title="Guinea-Bissau War of Independence">\n        war in Portuguese Guinea\n       </a>\n       that pitted 10,000\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">\n        Soviet Bloc\n       </a>\n       -supported PAIGC soldiers against 35,000 Portuguese and African troops.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn_14-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bn-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       By 1972, the PAIGC controlled much of Portuguese Guinea despite the presence of the Portuguese troops, but the organization did not attempt to disrupt Portuguese control in Cape Verde. Portuguese Guinea declared independence in 1973 and was granted\n       <a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">\n        de jure\n       </a>\n       independence in 1974. A budding independence movement\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 originally led by\n       <a href="/wiki/Am%C3%ADlcar_Cabral" title="Am\xc3\xadlcar Cabral">\n        Am\xc3\xadlcar Cabral\n       </a>\n       , assassinated in 1973\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 passed on to his half-brother\n       <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_Cabral" title="Lu\xc3\xads Cabral">\n        Lu\xc3\xads Cabral\n       </a>\n       and culminated in independence for the archipelago in 1975.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Independence_(1975)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_.281975.29">\n        Independence (1975)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Independence (1975)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stamps_of_Germany_(DDR)_1978,_MiNr_2293.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="835" data-file-width="710" height="259" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Stamps_of_Germany_%28DDR%29_1978%2C_MiNr_2293.jpg/220px-Stamps_of_Germany_%28DDR%29_1978%2C_MiNr_2293.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Stamps_of_Germany_%28DDR%29_1978%2C_MiNr_2293.jpg/330px-Stamps_of_Germany_%28DDR%29_1978%2C_MiNr_2293.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Stamps_of_Germany_%28DDR%29_1978%2C_MiNr_2293.jpg/440px-Stamps_of_Germany_%28DDR%29_1978%2C_MiNr_2293.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stamps_of_Germany_(DDR)_1978,_MiNr_2293.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Am%C3%ADlcar_Cabral" title="Am\xc3\xadlcar Cabral">\n          Am\xc3\xadlcar Cabral\n         </a>\n         on a stamp of the former\n         <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">\n          GDR\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Following the\n       <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">\n        April 1974 revolution in Portugal\n       </a>\n       , the PAIGC became an active political movement in Cape Verde. In December 1974, the PAIGC and Portugal signed an agreement providing for a transitional government composed of Portuguese and Cape Verdeans. On 30 June 1975, Cape Verdeans elected a National Assembly which received the instruments of independence from Portugal on 5 July 1975.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn_14-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bn-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the late 1970s and 1980s, most African countries prohibited\n       <a href="/wiki/South_African_Airways" title="South African Airways">\n        South African Airways\n       </a>\n       from overflights but Cape Verde allowed them and became a centre of activity for the airline\'s flights to Europe and the United States.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Immediately following the\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Guinea-Bissau#Independence_from_Portugal" title="History of Guinea-Bissau">\n        November 1980 coup in Guinea-Bissau\n       </a>\n       , relations between Cape Verde and Guinea-Bissau became strained. Cape Verde abandoned its hope for unity with Guinea-Bissau and formed the\n       <a href="/wiki/African_Party_for_the_Independence_of_Cape_Verde" title="African Party for the Independence of Cape Verde">\n        African Party for the Independence of Cape Verde\n       </a>\n       (PAICV). Problems have since been resolved and\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde%E2%80%93Guinea-Bissau_relations" title="Cape Verde\xe2\x80\x93Guinea-Bissau relations">\n        relations between the countries\n       </a>\n       are good. The PAICV and its predecessor established a one-party system and ruled Cape Verde from independence until 1990.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn_14-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bn-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Responding to growing pressure for pluralistic democracy, the PAICV called an emergency congress in February 1990 to discuss proposed constitutional changes to end one-party rule. Opposition groups came together to form the\n       <a href="/wiki/Movement_for_Democracy_(Cape_Verde)" title="Movement for Democracy (Cape Verde)">\n        Movement for Democracy\n       </a>\n       (MPD) in Praia in April 1990. Together, they campaigned for the right to contest the presidential election scheduled for December 1990.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The one-party state was abolished 28 September 1990, and the first multi-party elections were held in January 1991. The MPD won a majority of the seats in the National Assembly, and MPD presidential candidate\n       <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Mascarenhas_Monteiro" title="Ant\xc3\xb3nio Mascarenhas Monteiro">\n        Ant\xc3\xb3nio Mascarenhas Monteiro\n       </a>\n       defeated the PAICV\'s candidate with 73.5% of the votes. Legislative elections in December 1995 increased the MPD majority in the National Assembly. The party won 50 of the National Assembly\'s 72 seats.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A February 1996 presidential election returned President Monteiro to office. Legislative elections in January 2001 returned power to the PAICV, with the PAICV holding 40 of the National Assembly seats, MPD 30, and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Party_for_Democratic_Convergence" title="Party for Democratic Convergence">\n        Party for Democratic Convergence\n       </a>\n       (PCD) and\n       <a href="/wiki/Labour_and_Solidarity_Party" title="Labour and Solidarity Party">\n        Labour and Solidarity Party\n       </a>\n       (PTS) 1 each. In February 2001, the PAICV-supported presidential candidate\n       <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Pires" title="Pedro Pires">\n        Pedro Pires\n       </a>\n       defeated former MPD leader\n       <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Veiga" title="Carlos Veiga">\n        Carlos Veiga\n       </a>\n       by only 13 votes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn_14-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bn-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div style="clear:both;">\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">\n        Politics\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Politics">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Cape_Verde" title="Politics of Cape Verde">\n        Politics of Cape Verde\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Secretary_of_Defense_Chuck_Hagel,_right,_escorts_Cape_Verde_Prime_Minister_Jose_Maria_Neves_through_an_honor_cordon_and_into_the_Pentagon_on_March_28,_2013_130328-D-TT977-063.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2093" data-file-width="3145" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Secretary_of_Defense_Chuck_Hagel%2C_right%2C_escorts_Cape_Verde_Prime_Minister_Jose_Maria_Neves_through_an_honor_cordon_and_into_the_Pentagon_on_March_28%2C_2013_130328-D-TT977-063.jpg/250px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Secretary_of_Defense_Chuck_Hagel%2C_right%2C_escorts_Cape_Verde_Prime_Minister_Jose_Maria_Neves_through_an_honor_cordon_and_into_the_Pentagon_on_March_28%2C_2013_130328-D-TT977-063.jpg/375px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Secretary_of_Defense_Chuck_Hagel%2C_right%2C_escorts_Cape_Verde_Prime_Minister_Jose_Maria_Neves_through_an_honor_cordon_and_into_the_Pentagon_on_March_28%2C_2013_130328-D-TT977-063.jpg/500px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="250"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Secretary_of_Defense_Chuck_Hagel,_right,_escorts_Cape_Verde_Prime_Minister_Jose_Maria_Neves_through_an_honor_cordon_and_into_the_Pentagon_on_March_28,_2013_130328-D-TT977-063.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Cape Verdean Prime Minister\n         <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Maria_Neves" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Maria Neves">\n          Jos\xc3\xa9 Maria Neves\n         </a>\n         meets with the US Secretary of Defense\n         <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Hagel" title="Chuck Hagel">\n          Chuck Hagel\n         </a>\n         , in 2013.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Cape Verde is a stable\n       <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">\n        semi-presidential\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">\n        representative democratic\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">\n        republic\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SpL_4-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SpL-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-constitution_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-constitution-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is among the most democratic nations in the world, ranking 23rd position in the world, according to the\n       <i>\n        2016\n        <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">\n         Democracy Index\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a class="external text" href="https://www.constituteproject.org/constitution/Cape_Verde_1992?lang=en" rel="nofollow">\n        constitution\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x94 adopted in 1980 and revised in 1992, 1995 and 1999\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 defines the basic principles of its government. The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/President_of_Cape_Verde" title="President of Cape Verde">\n        president\n       </a>\n       is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">\n        head of state\n       </a>\n       and is elected by\n       <a href="/wiki/Direct_election" title="Direct election">\n        popular vote\n       </a>\n       for a 5-year term.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn_14-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bn-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Cape_Verde" title="Prime Minister of Cape Verde">\n        prime minister\n       </a>\n       is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">\n        head of government\n       </a>\n       and proposes other ministers and secretaries of state. The prime minister is nominated by the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Cape_Verde)" title="National Assembly (Cape Verde)">\n        National Assembly\n       </a>\n       and appointed by the president.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       Members of the National Assembly are elected by popular vote for 5-year terms. Three parties now hold seats in the National Assembly\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 MPD (36), PAICV (25) and the Cape Verdean Independent Democratic Union (UCID) (3).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yahoo.com_18-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-yahoo.com-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The judicial system consists of a Supreme Court of Justice\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 whose members are appointed by the president, the National Assembly, and the Board of the Judiciary\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 and regional courts. Separate courts hear civil, constitutional, and criminal cases. Appeal is to the Supreme Court.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn_14-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bn-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The two main political parties are PAICV and MPD.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yahoo.com_18-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-yahoo.com-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">\n        Foreign relations\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Cape_Verde" title="Foreign relations of Cape Verde">\n        Foreign relations of Cape Verde\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cape_Verdean_embassies.PNG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1425" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Cape_Verdean_embassies.PNG/250px-Cape_Verdean_embassies.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Cape_Verdean_embassies.PNG/375px-Cape_Verdean_embassies.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Cape_Verdean_embassies.PNG/500px-Cape_Verdean_embassies.PNG 2x" width="250"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cape_Verdean_embassies.PNG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Map of countries with Cape Verdean embassies\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Cape Verde follows a policy of\n       <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">\n        nonalignment\n       </a>\n       and seeks cooperative relations with all friendly states.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn_14-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bn-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">\n        Angola\n       </a>\n       , Brazil, the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People\'s Republic of China">\n        People\'s Republic of China\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">\n        Libya\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">\n        Cuba\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">\n        France\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">\n        Germany\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">\n        Portugal\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">\n        Spain\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">\n        Senegal\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">\n        Russia\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">\n        Luxembourg\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n        United States\n       </a>\n       maintain embassies in Praia.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn_14-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bn-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Cape Verde is actively interested in foreign affairs\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">\n          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (November 2016)">\n           clarification needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       , especially in Africa.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn_14-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bn-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Cape Verde has\n       <a href="/wiki/Bilateralism" title="Bilateralism">\n        bilateral relations\n       </a>\n       with some\n       <a href="/wiki/Lusophone" title="Lusophone">\n        Lusophone\n       </a>\n       nations and holds membership in a number of international organisations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn_14-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bn-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It also participates in most international conferences on economic and political issues.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bn_14-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bn-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Since 2007, Cape Verde has a\n       <i>\n        special partnership\n       </i>\n       status\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       with the\n       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">\n        EU\n       </a>\n       , under the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cotonou_Agreement" title="Cotonou Agreement">\n        Cotonou Agreement\n       </a>\n       , and might apply for\n       <a href="/wiki/Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union#Cape_Verde" title="Future enlargement of the European Union">\n        special membership\n       </a>\n       , even because the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verdean_escudo" title="Cape Verdean escudo">\n        Cape Verdean escudo\n       </a>\n       , the country\'s currency, is indexed to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">\n        Euro\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2011 Cape Verde ratified the\n       <a href="/wiki/Rome_Statute_of_the_International_Criminal_Court" title="Rome Statute of the International Criminal Court">\n        Rome Statute of the International Criminal Court\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Military">\n        Military\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Military">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verdean_Armed_Forces" title="Cape Verdean Armed Forces">\n        Cape Verdean Armed Forces\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marins_du_Cap-Vert_en_2011.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="2100" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Marins_du_Cap-Vert_en_2011.jpg/220px-Marins_du_Cap-Vert_en_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Marins_du_Cap-Vert_en_2011.jpg/330px-Marins_du_Cap-Vert_en_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Marins_du_Cap-Vert_en_2011.jpg/440px-Marins_du_Cap-Vert_en_2011.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Marins_du_Cap-Vert_en_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Marines of the Cape Verdean Coast Guard\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verdean_Armed_Forces" title="Cape Verdean Armed Forces">\n        military of Cape Verde\n       </a>\n       consists of a National Guard and the Coast Guard.; 0.7% of the country\'s GDP was spent on the military in 2005.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Having fought their only\n       <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau_War_of_Independence" title="Guinea-Bissau War of Independence">\n        war for independence\n       </a>\n       against Portugal between 1974 and 1975, the efforts of the Caboverdean Armed Forces have now been turned to combating international drug trafficking. In 2007, together with the Cabo Verdean Police, they carried out Operation Flying Launch (\n       <i>\n        Operac\xc3\xa3o Lancha Voador\n       </i>\n       a), a successful operation to put an end to a drug trafficking group which smuggled cocaine from\n       <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">\n        Colombia\n       </a>\n       to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">\n        Netherlands\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">\n        Germany\n       </a>\n       using the country as a reorder point. The operation took more than three years, being a secret operation during the first two years, and ended in 2010.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Although located in Africa, Cape Verde has always had close relations with Europe. Because of this, some scholars argue that Cape Verde may be eligible to join the\n       <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">\n        Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">\n        NATO\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The most recent engagement of the Armed Forces was the\n       <a href="/wiki/Monte_Tchota_massacre" title="Monte Tchota massacre">\n        Monte Tchota massacre\n       </a>\n       that resulted in 11 deaths.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="International_recognition">\n        International recognition\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: International recognition">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Cape Verde is often praised\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       as an example among African nations for its stability and developmental growth despite its lack of natural resources. Among other achievements, it has been recognised with the following assessments:\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable sortable">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Index\n        </th>\n   </table>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">\n        Geography\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Cape_Verde" title="Geography of Cape Verde">\n        Geography of Cape Verde\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Topographic_map_of_Cape_Verde-en.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1087" data-file-width="1464" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Topographic_map_of_Cape_Verde-en.svg/220px-Topographic_map_of_Cape_Verde-en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Topographic_map_of_Cape_Verde-en.svg/330px-Topographic_map_of_Cape_Verde-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Topographic_map_of_Cape_Verde-en.svg/440px-Topographic_map_of_Cape_Verde-en.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Topographic_map_of_Cape_Verde-en.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A\n         <a href="/wiki/Topographic_map" title="Topographic map">\n          topographic map\n         </a>\n         of Cape Verde\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cape_Verde.2010-11-23.250m-per-px.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2200" data-file-width="2800" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Cape_Verde.2010-11-23.250m-per-px.jpg/220px-Cape_Verde.2010-11-23.250m-per-px.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Cape_Verde.2010-11-23.250m-per-px.jpg/330px-Cape_Verde.2010-11-23.250m-per-px.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Cape_Verde.2010-11-23.250m-per-px.jpg/440px-Cape_Verde.2010-11-23.250m-per-px.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cape_Verde.2010-11-23.250m-per-px.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A satellite photo of the Cape Verde islands, 2010\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The Cape Verde archipelago is in the Atlantic Ocean, approximately 570 kilometres (350\xc2\xa0mi) off the western coast of the African continent, near Senegal, The Gambia, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">\n        Mauritania\n       </a>\n       , and is part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Macaronesia" title="Macaronesia">\n        Macaronesia\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">\n        ecoregion\n       </a>\n       . It lies between latitudes\n       <a href="/wiki/14th_parallel_north" title="14th parallel north">\n        14\xc2\xb0\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/18th_parallel_north" title="18th parallel north">\n        18\xc2\xb0N\n       </a>\n       , and longitudes\n       <a href="/wiki/22nd_meridian_west" title="22nd meridian west">\n        22\xc2\xb0\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/26th_meridian_west" title="26th meridian west">\n        26\xc2\xb0W\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The country is a horseshoe-shaped cluster of ten islands (nine inhabited) and eight islets,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_27-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pc-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       that constitute an area of 4033\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_27-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pc-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The islands are spatially divided into two groups:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <a href="/wiki/Barlavento_Islands" title="Barlavento Islands">\n         Barlavento Islands\n        </a>\n        (\n        <a href="/wiki/Windward_and_leeward" title="Windward and leeward">\n         windward\n        </a>\n        islands):\n        <a href="/wiki/Santo_Ant%C3%A3o,_Cape_Verde" title="Santo Ant\xc3\xa3o, Cape Verde">\n         Santo Ant\xc3\xa3o\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Vicente,_Cape_Verde" title="S\xc3\xa3o Vicente, Cape Verde">\n         S\xc3\xa3o Vicente\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Santa_Luzia,_Cape_Verde" title="Santa Luzia, Cape Verde">\n         Santa Luzia\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Nicolau,_Cape_Verde" title="S\xc3\xa3o Nicolau, Cape Verde">\n         S\xc3\xa3o Nicolau\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Sal,_Cape_Verde" title="Sal, Cape Verde">\n         Sal\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Boa_Vista,_Cape_Verde" title="Boa Vista, Cape Verde">\n         Boa Vista\n        </a>\n        ;\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_27-2">\n         <a href="#cite_note-pc-27">\n          [27]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        and\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <a href="/wiki/Sotavento_Islands" title="Sotavento Islands">\n         Sotavento Islands\n        </a>\n        (\n        <a href="/wiki/Windward_and_leeward" title="Windward and leeward">\n         leeward\n        </a>\n        ):\n        <a href="/wiki/Maio,_Cape_Verde" title="Maio, Cape Verde">\n         Maio\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Santiago,_Cape_Verde" title="Santiago, Cape Verde">\n         Santiago\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Fogo,_Cape_Verde" title="Fogo, Cape Verde">\n         Fogo\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Brava,_Cape_Verde" title="Brava, Cape Verde">\n         Brava\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_27-3">\n         <a href="#cite_note-pc-27">\n          [27]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       The largest island, both in size and population, is Santiago, which hosts the nation\'s capital, Praia, the principal urban agglomeration in the archipelago.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_27-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pc-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Three of the Cape Verde islands, Sal, Boa Vista and Maio, are fairly flat, sandy, and dry; the others are generally rockier with more vegetation.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_geography_and_geology">\n        Physical geography and geology\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Physical geography and geology">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Geologically, the islands, covering a combined area of slightly over 4,033 square kilometres (1,557 square miles), are principally composed of\n       <a href="/wiki/Igneous_rock" title="Igneous rock">\n        igneous rocks\n       </a>\n       , with volcanic structures and\n       <a href="/wiki/Pyroclastic_rock" title="Pyroclastic rock">\n        pyroclastic\n       </a>\n       debris comprising the majority of the archipelago\'s total volume. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">\n        volcanic\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Pluton" title="Pluton">\n        plutonic rocks\n       </a>\n       are distinctly basic; the archipelago is a soda-alkaline\n       <a href="/wiki/Petrography" title="Petrography">\n        petrographic\n       </a>\n       province, with a\n       <a href="/wiki/Petrology" title="Petrology">\n        petrologic\n       </a>\n       succession similar to that found in other\n       <a href="/wiki/Macaronesia" title="Macaronesia">\n        Macaronesian\n       </a>\n       islands.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Magnetic anomalies identified in the vicinity of the archipelago indicate that the structures forming the islands date back 125\xe2\x80\x93150 million years: the islands themselves date from 8 million (in the west) to 20 million years (in the east).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pim_et_al..2C_2008.2C_p.422_28-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Pim_et_al..2C_2008.2C_p.422-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The oldest exposed rocks occurred on Maio and northern peninsula of Santiago and are 128\xe2\x80\x93131 million year old pillow lavas. The first stage of volcanism in the islands began in the early\n       <a href="/wiki/Miocene" title="Miocene">\n        Miocene\n       </a>\n       , and reached its peak at the end of this period, when the islands reached their maximum sizes. Historical volcanism (within human settlement) has been restricted to the island of Fogo.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The origin of the islands\' volcanism has been attributed to a\n       <a href="/wiki/Hotspot_(geology)" title="Hotspot (geology)">\n        hotspot\n       </a>\n       , associated with bathymetric swell that formed the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde_Rise" title="Cape Verde Rise">\n        Cape Verde Rise\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Rise is one of the largest protuberances in the world\'s oceans, rising 2.2 kilometres (1.4 miles) in a semi-circular region of 1200\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       , associated with a rise of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Geoid" title="Geoid">\n        geoid\n       </a>\n       and elevated surface heat flow.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pim_et_al..2C_2008.2C_p.422_28-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Pim_et_al..2C_2008.2C_p.422-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Most recently erupting in 2014,\n       <a href="/wiki/Pico_do_Fogo" title="Pico do Fogo">\n        Pico do Fogo\n       </a>\n       is the largest active\n       <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">\n        volcano\n       </a>\n       in the region. It has a 8 kilometres (5 miles) diameter\n       <a href="/wiki/Caldera" title="Caldera">\n        caldera\n       </a>\n       , whose rim is 1,600 metres (5,249 feet) altitude and an interior cone that rises to 2,829 metres (9,281 feet)\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_sea_level" title="Above sea level">\n        above sea level\n       </a>\n       . The caldera resulted from subsidence, following the partial evacuation (eruption) of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Magma" title="Magma">\n        magma\n       </a>\n       chamber, along a cylindrical column from within magma chamber (at a depth of 8 kilometres (5 miles)).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Extensive\n       <a href="/wiki/Salt_pan_(geology)" title="Salt pan (geology)">\n        salt flats\n       </a>\n       are found on Sal and Maio.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_27-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pc-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On Santiago, Santo Ant\xc3\xa3o, and S\xc3\xa3o Nicolau, arid slopes give way in places to sugarcane fields or banana plantations spread along the base of towering mountains.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_27-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pc-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Ocean cliffs have been formed by catastrophic\n       <a href="/wiki/Landslide#Debris_landslide" title="Landslide">\n        debris landslides\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       According to the president of\n       <a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru">\n        Nauru\n       </a>\n       , Cape Verde has been ranked the eighth most endangered nation due to flooding from\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">\n        climate change\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n       <li    Santiago\n           </a>\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">\n        Climate\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Cape_Verde#Climate" title="Geography of Cape Verde">\n        Geography of Cape Verde \xc2\xa7\xc2\xa0Climate\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Cape Verde\'s climate is milder than that of the African mainland, because the surrounding sea moderates temperatures on the islands and cold Atlantic currents produce an arid atmosphere around the archipelago. Conversely, the islands do not receive the upwellings (cold streams) that affect the West African coast, so the air temperature is cooler than in Senegal, but the sea is warmer, because the orographic relief of some islands, such as Santiago with steep mountains, cover it with rich woods and luxuriant vegetation where the humid air condenses and soak the plants, rocks, soil, logs, moss, etc. On the higher islands and somewhat wetter islands, exclusively in mountainous areas, like Santo Ant\xc3\xa3o island, the climate is suitable for the development of dry monsoon forest, and laurel forest as this vegetation\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_27-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pc-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Average daily high temperatures range from 26\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (79\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F) in February to 31\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C (87.8\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F) in September.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VoodooSkies.com_32-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-VoodooSkies.com-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Cape Verde is part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">\n        Sahelian arid belt\n       </a>\n       , with nothing like the rainfall levels of nearby West Africa.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_27-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pc-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It rains irregularly between August and October, with frequent brief heavy downpours.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc_27-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pc-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A\n       <i>\n        desert\n       </i>\n       is usually defined as terrain that receives less than 250\xc2\xa0mm (9.8\xc2\xa0in) of annual rainfall. Sal\'s total of (145\xc2\xa0mm (5.7\xc2\xa0in)) confirms this classification. Most of the year\'s rain falls in September.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metoffice.gov.uk_33-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-metoffice.gov.uk-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable collapsible" style="width:90%; color:#000000; border-left-width:medium">\n         3,457.5\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="14" style="text-align:center;font-size:95%;">\n         Source #1: Weatherbase.com (humidity, sun and mean temperature),\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n          <a href="#cite_note-34">\n           [34]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         Met Office for precipitation\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metoffice.gov.uk_33-1">\n          <a href="#cite_note-metoffice.gov.uk-33">\n           [33]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="14" style="text-align:center; font-size:95%;">\n         Source #2: Voodoo Skies for the rest\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VoodooSkies.com_32-1">\n          <a href="#cite_note-VoodooSkies.com-32">\n           [32]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       Sal, Boa Vista and Maio have a flat landscape and arid climate, the remaining ones are generally rockier and have more vegetation. Because of the infrequent occurrence of rainfall the landscape is arid. The archipelago can be divided into four broad ecological zones\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\x94 arid, semiarid, subhumid and humid, according to altitude and average annual rainfall ranging from 200 millimetres (7.9 inches) in the arid areas of the coast to more than 1,000 millimetres (39 inches) in the humid mountain. Most rainfall precipitation is due to condensation of the ocean mist.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In some islands, as\n       <a href="/wiki/Santiago,_Cape_Verde" title="Santiago, Cape Verde">\n        Santiago\n       </a>\n       , the wetter climate of the interior and the eastern coast contrasts with the dryer one in the south/southwest coast. Praia, on the southeast coast, is the largest city of the island and the largest city and capital of the country.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Because of their proximity to the Sahara, most of the Cape Verde islands are dry, but on islands with high mountains and farther away from the coast, by orography, the humidity is much higher, providing a rainforest habitat, although much affected by the human presence. Northeastern slopes of high mountains often receive a lot of rain while southwest slopes do not. These umbria areas are identified with cool and moisture.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Western Hemisphere-bound hurricanes often have their early beginnings near the Cape Verde Islands. These are referred to as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Verde-type_hurricane" title="Cape Verde-type hurricane">\n        Cape Verde-type hurricanes\n       </a>\n       . These hurricanes can become very intense as they cross warm Atlantic waters away from Cape Verde. The average hurricane season has about two Cape Verde-type hurricanes, which are usually the largest and most intense storms of the season because they often have plenty of warm open ocean over which to develop before encountering land. The five largest Atlantic tropical cyclones on record have been Cape Verde-type hurricanes. Most of the longest-lived tropical cyclones in the Atlantic basin are Cape Verde hurricanes.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The islands themselves have only been struck by hurricanes twice in recorded history (since 1851): once in 1892, and again in 2015 by\n       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Fred_(2015)" title="Hurricane Fred (2015)">\n        Hurricane Fred\n       </a>\n       , the easternmost hurricane ever to form in the Atlantic.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Biome">\n        Biome\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Biome">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Cape_Verde" title="Wildlife of Cape Verde">\n        Wildlife of Cape Verde\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Cape Verde\'s isolation has resulted in the islands having a number of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endemic_(ecology)" title="Endemic (ecology)">\n        endemic\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">\n        species\n       </a>\n       , particularly bird and reptiles, many of which are\n       <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">\n        endangered\n       </a>\n       by human development. Endemic birds include\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexander%27s_swift" title="Alexander\'s swift">\n        Alexander\'s swift\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        Apus alexandri\n       </i>\n       ),\n       <a href="/wiki/Bourne%27s_heron" title="Bourne\'s heron">\n        Bourne\'s heron\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        Ardea purpurea bournei\n       </i>\n       ), the\n       <a href="/wiki/Raso_lark" title="Raso lark">\n        Raso lark\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        Alauda razae\n       </i>\n       ), the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde_warbler" title="Cape Verde warbler">\n        Cape Verde warbler\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        Acrocephalus brevipennis\n       </i>\n       ), and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Iago_sparrow" title="Iago sparrow">\n        Iago sparrow\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        Passer iagoensis\n       </i>\n       ).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The islands are also an important breeding area for seabirds including the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde_shearwater" title="Cape Verde shearwater">\n        Cape Verde shearwater\n       </a>\n       . Reptiles include the Cape Verde giant gecko (\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Tarentola" title="Tarentola">\n         Tarentola\n        </a>\n        gigas\n       </i>\n       ).\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">\n        Administrative divisions\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Verde&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Cabo_Verde" title="Administrative divisions of Cabo Verde">\n        Administrative divisions of Cabo Verde\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Cape Verde is divided into 22\n       <a href="/wiki/Municipality" title="Municipality">\n        municipalities\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        concelhos\n       </i>\n       ) and subdivided into 32 parishes (\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freguesia_(Portugal)" title="Freguesia (Portugal)">\n         freguesias\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ), based on the religious parishes that existed during the colonial period:\n      </p>\n      <div>\n       <table class="wikitable">\n        <caption>\n
